# Data Model: mangaMaps


2D maps of DAP measured properties.


## Contents
- [Basic Information](#basic-information)
- [Changelog](#changelog)
- [Example HDUS List](#example-hdus-list)
- [Notes](#notes)
- [Regrets](#regrets)
---

## Basic Information
"""The MAPS files are the primary output file from the DAP and provide 2D "maps" (i.e., images)
of DAP measured properties. The shape and WCS of these images identically match that of a
single wavelength channel in the corresponding DRP LOGCUBE file.
Most properties are provided in groups of three fits extensions:

    [property]: the measurement value,
    [property]_IVAR: the measurement uncertainty stored as the inverse variance
    [property]_MASK: a corresponding bit mask for each pixel.

Extensions can either be a single 2D image or they can have a series of images that are organized along the third dimension. For the latter, each image is said to be in a specific "channel." For example, each Gaussian-fitted emission-line flux is provided in a single channel in the EMLINE_GFLUX extension. The headers of all the main data extensions include:

    the WCS information,
    the HDUCLASS keyword block,
    the channel (and unit) descriptions for the multichannel extensions,
    the name of the relevant maskbit group --- for the MAPS file, this is always MANGA_DAPPIXMASK,
    the units for any single image or datacube extensions (BUNIT), and
    the DATASUM and CHECKSUM values."""


### Naming Convention
manga-[plate]-[ifudesign]-MAPS-[daptype].fits.gz, where [plate] is the plate number, [ifudesign] is the design IFU size and number, and [daptype] is the shorthand keyword for the specific configuration of the analysis procedures performed by the DAP. The combined [plate]-[ifudesign] is also known as the PLATEIFU designation of a given galaxy. Note that the available [daptype]s have changed between DR16 and DR17; more information is provided in the data release documentation.

### Releases
DR15, DR16, DR17

### Enviroments
MANGA_SPECTRO_ANALYSIS

### Approximate Size
607 KB

### File Type
FITS

### Generated by Product
mangadap - manga_dap

### Is a VAC
False

### Data Level
2.1.0

## Changelog
Describes changes to the datamodel product and/or file structure from one release to another
 - DR17
   - from: DR16
   - added_hdus: ['SPECINDEX_WGT_CORR', 'EMLINE_SEW_CNT', 'SPECINDEX_WGT_MASK', 'SPECINDEX_BF_MODEL', 'SPECINDEX_BF', 'EMLINE_GEW_CNT', 'SPECINDEX_BF_IVAR', 'STELLAR_FOM', 'EMLINE_FOM', 'SPECINDEX_BF_CORR', 'SPECINDEX_MODEL', 'EMLINE_LFOM', 'SPECINDEX_WGT_MODEL', 'SPECINDEX_WGT_IVAR', 'EMLINE_GANR', 'SPECINDEX_WGT', 'EMLINE_GA', 'SPECINDEX_BF_MASK']
   - removed_hdus: ['STELLAR_CONT_FRESID', 'STELLAR_CONT_RCHI2']
   - primary_delta_nkeys: 1
   - added_primary_header_kwargs: ['PPXFFILT', 'VERSVBIN', 'VERSPPXF']
   - removed_primary_header_kwargs: ['STCKRES', 'STCKPRE']
 - DR16
   - from: DR15
   - note: No changes

### HDU1: SPX_SKYCOO
Sky-right offsets in arcsec -- +x toward +RA and +y toward +DEC -- of each spaxel from the galaxy center as determined using the OBJRA and OBJDEC keywords in the primary header.

#### HDU Size:  9 KB

### HDU2: SPX_ELLCOO
Elliptical polar coordinates of each spaxel from the galaxy center based on the on-sky coordinates in SPX_SKYCOO and the ECOOPA and ECOOELL parameters (typically taken from the NASA-Sloan atlas) in the primary header. In the limit of tilted, infinitely thin disk, these are the in-plane disk radius and azimuth; the 2nd channel is the radius normalized by the elliptical Petrosian effective radius from the NASA-Sloan atlas. In DR15/16, this extension includes the radius in arcsec and in units of Reff, and the in-plane (cylindrical) azimuth; DR17 also includes the radius in units of h-1 kpc.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  18 KB

##### Header Table Caption for HDU2

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| XTENSION | IMAGE | Image extension |

### HDU3: SPX_MFLUX
The g-band-weighted mean flux in each spaxel, not corrected for Galactic extinction or internal attenuation. Units are 10-17 erg/s/cm2/Å/spaxel.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  4 KB

### HDU6: BINID
Numerical ID for spatial bins for the binned spectra, stellar-continuum results, emission-line moment results, emission-line model results, and spectral-index results. It is important to understand that not all of the data in the MAPS are independent. In addition to covariance, measurements are repeated for a given binned spectrum in all the spaxels associated with that bin. Therefore, if you are, e.g., fitting a model to the MAPS data or calculating azimuthal averages, you should pull out the binned quantities that are unique before proceeding. In addition to any associated MASK values, you should use the BINID extension (and, indeed, its main purpose is) to extract the unique (but still correlated) data to use in such an analysis.
This extension has one channel for each of the 5 main processing steps... binning, stellar-continuum and -kinematics fitting, emission-line moment measurements, emission-line Gaussian modeling, and spectral indices. Keep in mind the following...
BINID == -1 means that the spaxel was not included in the analysis. For example, BINID values of -1 in the first BINID channel means that either the spaxel had insufficiently good/unmasked pixels or too low S/N to be included in the binning procedure. Any spaxel with BINID = -1 should also be masked as DONOTUSE in the respective property map.
A BINID may be >-1 in one channel and = -1 in a different channel. For example, a spaxel in the binning BINID map may be >-1 but be = -1 in the stellar-continuum BINID. This likely means that the spaxels were successfully binned, but the bin had S/N < 1 meaning it was not analyzed by the stellar-continuum fitting module.
For the VOR binning case, the only difference in BINIDs is the -1 vs. non-negative distinction described in the last point, except for the HYB binning scheme. For the HYB binning case, the emission-line moments, emission-line modeling, and spectral-index measurements are done on a spaxel-by-spaxel basis, meaning that the BINIDs are redetermined and is just a running number for the spaxels that were analyzed.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  22 KB

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

### HDU8: BIN_LWELLCOO
Light-weighted elliptical polar coordinates of each bin from the galaxy center based on the on-sky coordinates in BIN_LWSKYCOO and the ECOOPA and ECOOELL parameters (typically taken from the NASA-Sloan atlas) in the primary header. In the limit of tilted, infinitely thin disk, these are the in-plane disk radius and azimuth; the 2nd channel is the radius normalized by the elliptical Petrosian effective radius from the NASA-Sloan atlas. In DR15/16, this extension includes the radius in arcsec and in units of Reff, and the in-plane (cylindrical) azimuth; DR17 also includes the radius in units of h-1 kpc.

### HDU18: STELLAR_SIGMA
Raw line-of-sight stellar velocity dispersion measurements in km/s. These must be corrected using the data in the STELLAR_SIGMACORR extension to obtain the astrophysical dispersion! Instructions for applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. In DR17, the STELLAR_SIGMACORR extension has two channels; use the data in the first channel!

### HDU21: STELLAR_SIGMACORR
Quadrature correction for STELLAR_SIGMA to obtain the astrophysical velocity dispersion. Instructions for applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. In DR17, the STELLAR_SIGMACORR extension has two channels; use the data in the first channel! Advice for how to handle measurements that are smaller than the provided quadrature correction is provided in Sections 7.7 of Westfall et al. (2019, AJ, 158,231).

### HDU22: STELLAR_FOM
Provides provides 9 figures-of-merit for the stellar-continuum fit. The provided assessments are... (1) RMS of residuals (in 10-17 erg/s/cm2/Å/spaxel), (2) RMS of fractional residuals, (3) reduced chi-square, (4-6) 68th and 99th percentile and maximum value of fractional residuals, and (7-9) 68th and 99th percentile and maximum value of error-normalized residual; i.e., (data-model)/error.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  40 KB

##### Header Table Caption for HDU22
Key | Value | Comment | |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| XTENSION | IMAGE | Image extension |
| BITPIX | -32 | array data type |
| NAXIS | 3 | number of array dimensions |
| NAXIS1 | 34 |  |
| NAXIS2 | 34 |  |
| NAXIS3 | 9 |  |
| PCOUNT | 0 | number of parameters |
| GCOUNT | 1 | number of groups |
| WCSAXES | 3 | Number of coordinate axes |
| CRPIX1 | 18.0 | Pixel coordinate of reference point |
| CRPIX2 | 18.0 | Pixel coordinate of reference point |
| CRPIX3 | 1.0 | Pixel coordinate of reference point |

### HDU23: EMLINE_SFLUX
Non-parametric summed flux obtained after subtracting the stellar-continuum model. The emission-line fluxes account for Galactic reddening using the E(B-V) reddening, extinction factor Rv, and specified extinction law as provided in the primary header (EBVGAL, RVGAL, GEXTLAW, respectively).

### HDU30: EMLINE_GFLUX
Gaussian profile integrated flux obtained from a combined continuum+emission-line fit. The emission-line fluxes account for Galactic reddening using the E(B-V) reddening, extinction factor Rv, and specified extinction law as provided in the primary header (EBVGAL, RVGAL, GEXTLAW, respectively). The flux ratio of the [NeIII], [OIII], [OI], [NII], and [S III] lines are fixed.

### HDU37: EMLINE_GVEL
Line-of-sight velocity in km/s of the ionized gas relative to the input guess redshift, which is given as cz in SCINPVEL in the PRIMARY header and most often identical to the NSA redshift. The velocities of all lines are tied during the fitting process and cannot be treated as independent measurements! This means that all channels in this extension effectively provide identical information. The only difference is that some measurements may be flagged for some lines and not for others depending on the result of the dispersion fit.

#### HDU Size:  158 KB

### HDU40: EMLINE_GSIGMA
Gaussian profile velocity dispersion as would be measured from a direct Gaussian
fit to the emission lines. These must be corrected using the data in the
EMLINE_INSTSIGMA to obtain the astrophysical dispersion! Instructions for
applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the
MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. The velocity dispersions of the [OII], [NeIII],
HeI+Hζ, [OIII], [NI], [OI], [NII], and [SIII] lines are tied and cannot be treated
as independent measurements.

### HDU43: EMLINE_INSTSIGMA
The instrumental dispersion in km/s at the fitted center of each emission line. Use the data in this extension to correct the measured line dispersions provided by EMLINE_GSIGMA for the instrumental line-spread function.

### HDU44: EMLINE_TPLSIGMA
We fit the emission lines using pPXF using a set of emission-line templates. Given the varying spectral resolution of the MaNGA data, we setup these templates to have a non-zero "template instrumental dispersion" that is the same as the MaNGA instrumental disperison up to some quadrature offset. This extension provides the "template instrumental dispersion" at the location of each emission line. The velocity dispersion actually measured and returned by pPXF is the quadrature difference between the measurements in EMLINE_GSIGMA and the data in this extension. These data are provided for reference only. Use the data in EMLINE_INSTSIGMA to correct EMLINE_GSIGMA for the instrumental line-spread function, not the data provided in this extension!

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  158 KB

### HDU46: EMLINE_GANR
Provides the ratio of the Gaussian line amplitude to the median of the noise in two sidebands near each fitted emission line. The sideband uses are identical to those used for the equivalent-width measurements.

### HDU47: EMLINE_FOM
Provides 9 figures-of-merit for the continuum+emission-line fit. The provided assessments are... (1) RMS of residuals (in 10-17 erg/s/cm2/Å/spaxel), (2) RMS of fractional residuals, (3) reduced chi-square, (4-6) 68th and 99th percentile and maximum value of fractional residuals, and (7-9) 68th and 99th percentile and maximum value of error-normalized residual; i.e., (data-model)/error.

### HDU49: SPECINDEX
Absorption-line and bandhead/color index measurements made directly on the MaNGA spectra, after subtracting the best-fitting emission-line model. Measurements are in the rest frame. The definition of the absorption-line indices follow the classic method, as defined by Worthey et al. (1994, ApJS, 95, 107) and Trager et al. (1998, ApJS, 116, 1). See additional discussion regarding the definition of the absorption-line indices in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. Corrections are provided in the SPECINDEX_CORR extension to convert these measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  207 KB

### HDU52: SPECINDEX_CORR
Corrections for the data in SPECINDEX that converts the index measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra. Instructions for applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. The corrections must be applied differently for indices of different units! For indices that are unitless or in units of angstrom, the corrected index follows SPECINDEX * SPECINDEX_CORR, meaning that the corrections are unitless. For indices in magnitude units, the corrected index follows SPECINDEX + SPECINDEX_CORR, meaning that the corrections have magnitude units.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  207 KB

### HDU53: SPECINDEX_MODEL
Provides absorption-line and bandhead/color index measurements made directly on the best-fitting continuum model spectrum for each MaNGA spectrum. Measurements are in the rest frame. The same corrections applied to SPECINDEX can be applied to these data to obtain the 0-velocity-dispersion measurement at the spectral resolution of the template spectra.

### HDU54: SPECINDEX_BF
Absorption-line and bandhead/color index measurements made directly on the MaNGA spectra, after subtracting the best-fitting emission-line model. Measurements are in the rest frame.

The definition of the absorption-line indices follows a definition similar to Burstein et al. (1984, ApJ, 287, 586) and Faber et al. (1985, ApJS, 57, 711). Absorption-line indices defined in this way ensure mathematically identical calculations when aggregating measured index values and measurements determined from spectral stacks; aggregations require the use of the weights provided by the SPECINDEX_WGT extension. See additional discussion regarding the definition of the absorption-line indices in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation.

Corrections are provided in the SPECINDEX_BF_CORR extension to convert these measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra.

### HDU57: SPECINDEX_BF_CORR
Corrections for the data in SPECINDEX_BF that converts the index measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra. Instructions for applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation. The corrections must be applied differently for indices of different units!

For indices that are unitless or in units of angstrom, the corrected index follows SPECINDEX * SPECINDEX_CORR, meaning that the corrections are unitless. For indices in magnitude units, the corrected index follows SPECINDEX + SPECINDEX_CORR, meaning that the corrections have magnitude units.

### HDU58: SPECINDEX_BF_MODEL
Provides absorption-line and bandhead/color index measurements made directly on the best-fitting continuum model spectrum for each MaNGA spectrum. Measurements are in the rest frame. The same corrections applied to SPECINDEX_BF can be applied to these data to obtain the 0-velocity-dispersion measurement at the spectral resolution of the template spectra.

### HDU59: SPECINDEX_WGT
Weights to be used with the SPECINDEX_BF measurements to correctly aggregate measurements into a single, higher-S/N measurement. Weights are all unitless. See additional discussion regarding the definition of the absorption-line indices and the use of these weights in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation.

Corrections are provided in the SPECINDEX_WGT_CORR extension to convert these measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra.

### HDU62: SPECINDEX_WGT_CORR
Corrections for the data in SPECINDEX_WGT that converts the measurements to 0 velocity dispersion at the spectral resolution of the template spectra. Instructions for applying these corrections are provided in the data release documentation and the MaNGA DAP ReadTheDocs Documentation.

#### HDU Type: IMAGE
#### HDU Size:  207 KB

### HDU63: SPECINDEX_WGT_MODEL
Provides the aggregation weights as measured using the best-fitting continuum model.

#### HDU Size:  207 KB
